Jamison Brereton

19 (535)
Indra
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The first half of this hymn (vss. 1тАУ5) celebrates various victories of Indra, giving aid both to men of the mythic past (e.g., Kutsa, vs. 2) and those of the present, especially King Sud─Бs (vss. 3, also 6), the leader also in the Battle of the Ten Kings treated in the preceding, well-known hymn (VII.18). The allegiances and enmities of that hymn are strikingly different here: for example, Indra helps the P┼лru king in this hymn (vs. 3), whereas in VII.18 the P┼лrus are the enemy.
Beginning with verse 6 we attempt to mobilize the powers and protection that Indra has previously provided for us, and as usual we offer praise in return.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra

рдпрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рддрд┐рдЧреНрдорд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧрдГ рддреАрдХреНрд╖реНрдгрд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧрдГ рд╡реГрд╖рднреЛ рди рд╡реГрд╖рдн рдЗрд╡ рднреАрдордГ рднрдпрдВрдХрд░рдГ рд╕рдиреН рдПрдХрдГ рдЕрд╕рд╣рд╛рдп рдПрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреАрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдЬрдирд╛рдиреН рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░ рдЪреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдпрддрд┐ ред рдпрдГ рдЪреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЕрджрд╛рд╢реБрд╖рдГ рдЕрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╢рд╢реНрд╡рддрдГ рдмрд╣реЛрдГ рдЧрдпрд╕реНрдп рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдп рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрдкрд╣рд░реНрддрд╛ рднрд╡рддреАрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖: ред рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реБрд╖реНрд╡рд┐рддрд░рд╛рдп рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рд╕реЛрдорд╛рднрд┐рд╖рд╡рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреЗ рдЬрдирд╛рдп рд╡реЗрджрдГ рдзрдирдВ рдкреНрд░рдпрдиреНрддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рджрд╛рддрд╛ рдЕрд╕рд┐ рее рддреГрдиреНрдирдиреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрддреНрд░ рд╖рд╖реНрдареНрдпрд╛ рдЕрднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рдЕрд╕рд┐ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдпрджреНрд╡реГрддреНрддрдпреЛрдЧрд╛рдЪреНрдЪрд╛рдиреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рд╕рдВрднрд╡рд╛рддреН рдпрджреНрд╡реГрддреНрддрдпреБрдХреНрддрдорд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдордзреНрдпрд╛рд╣реГрддреНрдп рдпреЛрдЬрдирд╛ рдХреГрддрд╛ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, who is formidable as a sharp-horned bull, singly expels all men (from their stations); you who arethe despoiler of the ample wealth of him who makes no offerings are the giver of riches to the presenter offrequent oblations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who, like a fearsome sharp-horned bull, alone rouses forth all the communities;
(you) who hold forth to the better (soma-)presser the patrimony and possessions of each and every impious manтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Rhetorically interesting to begin a hymn with a syntactically nonindependent verse. This verse consists only of relative clauses (pace Geldner; see below), which find their main clause referent in the first word of the 2nd verse (and indeed subsequent verses), namely tv├бm. Although тАШyouтАЩ clearly is the referent, the first relative clause of vs. 1 has a 3rd ps. verb (cy─Бv├бyati), though the second one switches to the 2nd person (prayant─Б╠Бsi). It might be possible to attribute the 3rd ps. in ab to attraction to the simile, but such a switch would be very rare.

The simile marker n├б in p─Бda a is wrongly placed, after the 2nd member of a three-word simile, not the first (tigm├б┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Еgo vс╣Ыс╣гabh├│ n├б bh─лm├бс╕е). Ordinarily, given such a structure, the first word would be interpreted as the common term and therefore not a part of the simile proper (тАЬsharp-horned like a fearsome bullтАЭ), but Indra doesnтАЩt have horns, which should certainly belong to the bull. The wrong position may result from the fact that X n├б bh─лm├б-, where X = an animal, appears to be a formulaic structure, esp. mс╣Ыg├б- n├б bh─лm├б- (I.154.2, 190.3, II.33.11, etc.; also siс╣Гh├б- n├б bh─лm├б- IV.16.14, IX.97.28 and others). This smaller fixed phrase would then be fitted into a simile containing another term.

Geldner takes p─Бda d as a main clause, following the Pp., which analyses prayant─Б╠Бsi as containing unaccented asi. But this requires him to invent a verb for the relative clause of c (тАЬraubstтАЭ) for which there is no support - and no need. Already Oldenberg suggested accenting ├бsi contrary to the Pp.

Oldenberg (see also Tichy) also notes the nice example of case disharmony, where both gen. g├бyasya and acc. v├йdaс╕е are objects of the agent noun prayant─Б╠Б. As has often been noted, suffix-accented -tar-stems generally have genitive complements, as opposed to root-accented ones, which generally take accusatives. But enough exceptions exist to allow prayant─Б╠Бto take both. That g├бyasya is parallel to v├йdaс╕е and not to ├бd─Б┼Ыuс╣гaс╕е is shown by passages like IX.23.3 тАж ├бd─Б┼Ыuс╣гo g├бyam and VIII.81.7 ├бd─Б┼Ы┼лс╣гtarasya v├йdaс╕е. It is possible, but not necessary, that prayant─Б╠Бsi is a periphrastic future. 15 I have no explanation for the comparative s├║с╣гvitara- тАШbetter soma-presserтАЩ, beyond the occasional use of the comparative for emphasis or intensification, without comparandum.

English translation:

тАЬAiding him with your person n, Indra, you had defended Kutsa in combat when you had subjugatedD─Бsa, ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa and Kuyava, giving (their spoil) to that son of Arjuni.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just you, o Indra, helped Kutsa, while seeking fame for yourself with your own body in the clash,
when for him you weakened the D─Бsa ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa bringing bad harvest, doing your best for ArjunaтАЩs offspring.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b is repeated in IV.38.7, there of Dadhikr─Б the racehorse. (This repetition is not noted in Bloomfield Rig-Veda Repetitions) Renou at IV.38.7 and Geldner here (but not there) take ┼Ы├║┼Ыr┼лс╣гam─Бnaс╕е as meaning something like тАЬputting oneself at the disposal (of someone else, here Kutsa).тАЭ I assume that they are thinking of the enlarged root тИЪ┼Ыruс╣г тАШbe obedientтАЩ, but the two meanings seem quite distinct to me - I canтАЩt see Indra being obedient to any man - and formally our participle is a well-formed desiderative to тИЪ┼Ыru. In both places I take it as meaning тАЬdesiring to be heard/famedтАЩ; here Indra also helps out Kutsa, but at least part of his aim is to ensure his own fame.

In IV.38.7 there is no subsidiary beneficiary, and so the focus on the subject and his fame is ever clearer. Heenen is similarly puzzled by Geldner (238 n. 263) but tr. тАЬ(toi qui) en personne as la volont├й dтАЩ├йcouter au combat,тАЭ attributing an active sense to the middle participle.

The word d─Б╠Бsam beginning c plays off both (├б)d─Б┼Ыuс╣гo in 1c and sud─Б╠Бsam in 3b.

Thou, verily, Indra, gavest help to Kutsa, willingly giving car to him in battle,
When, aiding Arjuneya, thou subduedst to him both Kuyava and the Dasa Susna.

Du, Indra, halfest dazumal dem Kutsa, selbst gegenw├дrtig ihn im Kampf erh├╢rend, Als ├Зuschna du, den D├дmon schlechter Ernte, dem Ardschuneja huldvoll ├╝bergabest.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUndaunted (Indra), you had protected with all your protections Sud─Бsa, the offerer of oblations; youhave protected in battles with enemies for the possession of the earth Trasadasyu, the son of Purukutsa, andPuru.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, o bold one, boldly helped on Sud─Бs, whose oblation is worth pursuing, with all forms of help;
you helped on Trasadasyu, son of Purukutsa, and P┼лru in the winning of land, in the smashing of obstacles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Trasadasyu and the P┼лrus also appear in IV.38 (vss. 1, 3), which contains the p─Бda in common with our 2b.

Griffith

O Bold One, thou with all thine aids hast boldly holpen Sudas whose offerings were accepted,
Puru in winning land and slaying foemen, and Trasadasyu son of Purukutsa.

Geldner

Du Mutiger halfst mutig mit allen Hilfen dem Sudas, dessen Opfer begehrt waren, weiter. Du halfst dem Trasadasyu, des Purukutsa Sohne, weiter, dem Puru bei dem Landerwerb in der Feindeschlacht.

Grassmann

Mit K├╝hnheit, k├╝hner, halfest du dem Sudas, mit aller H├╝lfe dem beliebten Opfrer, Dem Sohn des Purukutsi, Trasadasju, dem Puru auch zum Landerwerb in Schlachten.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, the lord of horses, who are honoured by men, have destroyed, along with the Maruts, numerousenemies at the sacrifice of the gods; you have put to sleep with the thunderbolt the Dasyus, Chumuri, and Dhuni,on behalf of Dabh─лti.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

YouтАФwhose mind is inclined toward men in their pursuit of the godsтАФ along with men you smash many obstacles, you of the fallow bays;
you put to sleep the Dasyu Cumuri and Dhuni, easy to smash, for
Dabh─лti.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse puts into analytic (that is, syntactically independent) form some expressions met as compounds in the previous verse. Most obvious is (bh┼л╠Бr─лс╣Зi) vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Б тАж haс╣Гsi, which realizes vс╣Ыtrah├бtyeс╣гu in 3d. (Notice that both refer to plural events, handling their grammatical plurality in different ways.) A real d├бsyu- is destroyed in 4cd, plucked from the name Trasadasyu in 3c. In a slightly different relationship, dev├бv─лtau тАШin pursuit of the godsтАЩ here contains a form of the root тИЪv─л тАШpursueтАЩ found as 1st compound member in v─лtahavyam тАШwhose oblation is worth pursuingтАЩ in 3a.

And within this verse nс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е doubles the first member of the next word, nс╣Ыmano.

Griffith

At the Gods’ banquet, hero-souled! with Heroes, Lord of Bay Steeds, thou slewest many foemen.
Thou sentest in swift death to sleep the Dasyu, both Cumuri and Dhuni, for Dabhiti.

Geldner

Du erschl├дgst mit den Mannen, du mannhaft Gesinnter, bei der G├╢tterladung viele Feinde, du Falbenlenker. Du hast den Dasyu Cumuri und Dhuni eingeschl├дfert, da├Я sie f├╝r Dabhiti leicht zu t├╢ten waren.

Grassmann

Durch M├дnner schl├дgst du mannhaft viele Feinde beim G├╢ttermahl, o Lenker goldner Rosse, Schnell t├╢dtend senktest du in Schlaf den D├дmon, den Tschumuri und Dhuni dem Dabhiti.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSuch, wielder of the thunderbolt, are your mighty powers, that when you had quickly destroyed ninetyand nine cities, you have occupied the hundredth as a plural ce of abode; you have slain Vс╣Ыtra, you have also slainNamuci.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Yours are these exploits, you with the mace in handтАФthat nine and ninety fortifications at once
along with the hundredth you worked to the end, in bringing them
to rest [=collapse]. You smashed Vr╠еtra, and moreover Namuci you
smashed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse presents some interlocking syntactic and lexical problems.

Unlike Geldner, I take p─Бdas b and c together. Splitting them requires him to supply a verb for b (тАЬbrachstтАЭ) again lacking support or necessity. Presumably again he is following the Pp, which analyzes ┼Ыatatam─Б╠Бviveс╣г─лс╕е as containing unaccented aviveс╣г─лс╕е.

I prefer to accent it and thus allow it to be the verb of the y├бd clause beginning in b.

In either case ┼Ыatatam─Б╠Бis a problem. Everyone wants it to be the 100th thing (probably p├║r- тАШfortificationтАЩ) that Indra destroys (after the 99 in b). Grassmann suggests reading ┼Ыatatam─Б╠Бm, which would provide the desired feminine accusative (agreeing with p├║r-), but among other things would damage the meter (since, s.v. viс╣г, he is still reading an augmented aviveс╣г─лс╕е). Geldner suggests that it [what is unspecified, presumably the sandhi agglomeration] is to be dissolved (тАЬaufzul├╢senтАЭ) into masc. ┼Ыatatam├бm, and the 100th thing that Indra destroys is ┼Ъambara himself. He makes no mention of meter, though this dissolution would cause the same metrical problem. Oldenberg suggests 16 supplying neut. pl. cyautn─Б╠Бni (without translating), but I donтАЩt see how an ordinal тАЬhundredthтАЭ can qualify all hundred items in the plural. There is a much simpler solution: to take ┼Ыatatam─Б╠Бas a feminine instrumental with the old ending -─Б.

Although Oldenberg claims (in arguing against Grassmann) that the fem. stem should be ┼Ыatatam─л╠Б-, this is simply wrong. See AiG II.2 ┬з457, which establishes -─Б as the rule and -─л as the rare exception. Cf. for -tama-stems purut├бm─Б- of Uс╣гas and m─Бtr╠е╠Бtam─Б-, and for ordinals the well-attested feminine pratham─Б╠Б-. Or, if Geldner is correct that the reference is to ┼Ъambara himself, ┼Ыatatam─Б╠Бcan be a masculine instr. sg. In either case the text can stand as it is, with no metrical or sandhi problems, and the syntax can be rescued.

Geldner takes niv├й┼Ыane in c as тАШat eveningтАЩ. The word generally means тАШcausing to settle downтАЩ (the usual association of -ana-nominals with the transitive-causative ├бya-formations) or, as a noun, тАШsettling downтАЩ, and is sometimes associated with SavitarтАЩs bringing the world to rest in the evening (IV.53.6, I.35.1, VI.71.2), an association that must have led to GeldnerтАЩs tr. But the word never otherwise means тАШeveningтАЩ. I read it with its full lexical value, but with a sinister edge. тАЬBringing them to restтАЭ is a euphemism like ├бsv─Бpayaс╕е тАШyou put to sleepтАЩ in 4d. Oldenberg mentions the тАЬgoing to restтАЭ possibility, but opts instead for тАЬin the dwelling place (of the enemy).тАЭ Again, there seems to me no reason for this attenuation of the meaning.

The root тИЪviс╣г means тАШwork, work overтАЩ, or here тАШwork to the endтАЩ, again used in a slightly euphemistic sense. Note the phonetic echo between niv├й┼Ыane and (a)viveс╣г─лr.

The d p─Бda is a perfect chiasmus, even to the positioning of a conjunction between verb and object: ├бha├▒ ca vс╣Ыtr├бm n├бmucim ut─Б╠Бhan. The mixture of ca and ut├б is curious. Klein (DGRV I.186-87) is not sure how to analyze it; he suggests either that itтАЩs a тАЬboth тАж andтАЭ type of construction, with each conjunction appearing 2nd in its phrase (or so I interpr. his lapidary disc.), or that тАЬca is a sentential conjunction adjoining d to the rest of the stanza, and ut├б conjoins the clauses of d.тАЭ I prefer the former.

Griffith

These were thy mighty powers that, Thunder-wielder, thou swiftly crushedst nine-and-ninety castles:
Thou capturedst the hundredth in thine onslaught; thou slewest Namuci, thou slewest Vrtra.

Grassmann

O Blitzestr├дger, das sind deine Thaten, dass du zerst├╢rtest neunundneunzig Burgen An einem Tag, die hundertste am Abend, und Vritra und den Namutschi erschlugest.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour favours, Indra, to Sud─Бsa, the donor (of offerings), the presenter of oblations, are infinite;showerer (of benefits), I yoke for you (your vigorous) steeds; may our prayers reach you who are mighty, towhom many rites are addressed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Win these delights of yours, Indra, for the pious Sud─Бs, who has given an oblation.
For you, the bull, I yoke the two bullish fallow bays. Let my sacred
formulations pursue the prize, o you of many talents.

Jamison Brereton Notes

s├бn─Б is generally taken (Grassmann, Geldner) as a neut. pl. adj. тАШoldтАЩ agreeing with bh├│jan─Бni, and this is certainly possible. I find the sentiment somewhat odd, however: to announce to Indra that the delights he has given to his client are тАЬoldтАЭ seems slighting. I prefer to interpret the word as the 2nd sg. act. impv. to тИЪsan тАШwinтАЩ; exactly this form occurs several times in initial position elsewhere. What gives me pause, however, is I.178.4, which contains very parallel phraseology, s├бn─Б t─Б╠Бte indra n├бvy─Б ─Б╠Бguс╕е, and where I do interpret s├бn─Б as тАШoldтАЩ. The difference there is that the poet contrasts the old deeds of Indra with the new ones (n├бvy─Б) that have come and so avoids insulting the god. In any case, either the тАШoldтАЩ or the тАШwinтАЩ interpretation is possible here, though I have a preference for the latter.

The oblation of Sud─БsтАЩs that was worth pursuing (v─лt├бhavyam) in vs. 3 has now been given by him (r─Бt├бhavy─Бya) here, tracking the progress of the sacrifice to the point of mutual benefit of man and god.

The phrase d─Б┼Ы├║с╣гe sud─Б╠Бse тАЬfor the pious Sud─БsтАЭ displays syllabic metathesis, d─Б-┼Ы┼л / su-d─Б, with neutralizing play on all three sibilants. The poet seems to like this 17 collocation: see comment above on vs. 2 for connections across three verses and below on VII.20.2.

Griffith

Old are the blessings, Indra, which thou gavest Sudas the worshipper who brought oblations.
For thee, the Strong, I yoke thy strong Bay Horses: may our prayers reach thee and win strength, Most Mighty!

Geldner

Alt sind deine Wohltaten f├╝r den opferspendenden, freigebigen Sudas, o Indra. Dir, dem Bullen, schirre ich die beiden bullenartigen Falben an. Meine Kraftworte sollen den Preis erstreben, du Vielverm├╢gender.

Grassmann

Das sind, o Indra, deine alten Gnaden, zu Lieb’ dem frommen Opferbringer Sudas, Dir schirr’ ich an, dem Stier, das goldne Stierpaar; dir, starker, m├╢gen Kraft Gebete bringen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬPowerful Indra, lord of horses, let us not be exposed at this ceremony, addressed to you, to themurderous despoiler; protect us with impregnable defences; may we be held dear among your worshippers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Being) within this enclosure of yours here, may we not be (available) to be delivered to evil, o mighty possessor of the fallow bays.
Protect us with defenses that keep the wolf away. May we be your dear ones, and dear to our patrons.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My construction of the first hemistich differs from GeldnerтАЩs, both with regard to the syntactic role of te and the sense of p├бriс╣гс╣нau and leads to a very different interpretation of the meaning. The latter word, literally тАШencirclementтАЩ, is generally taken as always negative, a tight spot or constriction (GeldnerтАЩs тАЬin dieser KlemmeтАЭ), but I find this interpretation hard to reconcile with the hic-et-nunc deictic asy─Б╠Бm, since the poet has given no indication that he is currently in distress. (GeldnerтАЩs note suggests that this is a memory of the situation in VII.18, the Ten Kings battle, but this seems to me an ill-supported attempt to account for the deictic.) I therefore think the p├бriс╣гс╣нihere is positive - IndraтАЩs encirclement (that is, protection) of us now - and te is to be construed with p├бriс╣гс╣нau: тАЬin this enclosure (that is, protection) of yours.тАЭ Weak support for this may be provided by the first p─Бda of the next verse, 8a, where тАж te тАж abh├нс╣гс╣нau# matches тАж te тАж p├бriс╣гс╣нau# here, with rhyming forms and identical morphology - and a parallel positive sense: тАЬin your charge.тАЭ There is also a parallel in the next hymn, in roughly the same part of the hymn, with te asy─Б╠Бm as here and a string of locatives: VII.20.8 тАж te asy─Б╠Бm sumata├║ тАжv├бr┼лthe тАж nс╣Ы╠Бp─лtau тАЬin this benevolence of yours, in your defense, in your protection for men.тАЭ In our passage Geldner (followed by Scarlatta 207) instead takes te as the subject of the infinitive par─Бda├н; in order to make this work he has recast the sentence from one with 1st person subject (m─Б╠БтАж bh┼лma тАЬmay we not beтАжтАЭ) to one with 2nd ps. subject: тАЬNicht sollst du uns тАж dem B├╢sen preisgaben.тАЭ ScarlattaтАЩs tr. maintains the syntactic structure of the original, but otherwise follows GeldnerтАЩs interpretation. Better is KeydanaтАЩs (Infinitive im с╣Ъgveda 156, 203) interpretation of par─Бda├н as a passive infinitive, as I take it - though he still takes te as the ultimate agent of the handing over. Again, I donтАЩt see that the poet has expressed any fear that Indra will betray them; rather, he hopes that the protection Indra provides them will keep any such ill-fortune from befalling them, a hope that is repeated in the next p─Бda.

The poetтАЩs penchant for case disharmony (see 1cd above) recurs in p─Бda d, where I read priy─Б╠Бsaс╕е both with gen. t├бva and with loc. s┼лr├нс╣гu.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe leader (of rites), reciters of prayers, offer, Maghavan, prayers devoutly for your adoration; they bytheir praises have appropriated the wealth of the niggards; select us (as the objects) of your friendship.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

By theirpraises: ye te havebhir vi p─Бс╣Зin ada┼Ыan: aprad─Бna┼Ы─лl─Бn vaс╣Зijo api dhan─Бni vi┼Ыeс╣гeс╣Зad─Бpayan, theyhave made to give, or have mulched, especially in their riches, those traders who are not donors of offerings

Jamison Brereton

Even now, all at once, o bounteous one, those in your charge, the men, the hymn-proclaimers, are proclaiming hymns,
they who by their invocations of you have distanced the niggards
through ritual service. Choose us for this same yoking [=ritual
companionship].

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take p─Бda c with ab, since all three have 3rd ps. subjects referring to IndraтАЩs worshipers and clients, with p─Бda c a rel. cl. beginning with y├й. Geldner, by contrast, connects c with d, although d now refers to the same people in the 1st ps.

(asm─Б╠Бn vс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣гva тАЬchoose usтАЭ). He does not, however, take asm─Б╠Бn as coreferential with the y├й of c, but rather apparently interprets the relationship between the clauses as a kind of improper relativization: тАЬfor the same alliance (y├║jy─Бya t├бsmai) as (those) who (y├й)тАжтАЭ This has the advantage of providing some reason for the final t├бsmai, which I find hard to account for, though I find his way of linking the clauses too tricky. Scarlatta takes the first p─Бda as a temporal subordinate clause (тАЬAs soon as they are in your charge, the menтАжтАЭ). This is worth considering, although I am dubious about the subordinating quality of sady├б┼Ы cid. In the end, although I am not entirely 18 certain of my own way of putting together the various elements in this verse, I have not been convinced by those of other tr. either.

Note the poetтАЩs playful variation on 8a тАж te maghavann abh├нс╣гс╣нau with тАж t├й maghavann abh├нс╣гс╣нau, where the simple addition of an accent turns the 2nd ps. sg. into a 3rd ps. pl.

n├бraс╕е ┼Ыaс╣Гsanti recalls the epithet n├бr─Б┼Ы├бс╣Гsa, and then participates in an interweaving of two words for ritual speech: ┼Ыaс╣Гsanti uktha┼Ы─Бsa ukth─Б╠Б.

The lexeme v├н тИЪd─Б┼Ы occurs only here, as far as I know. Like the idiom ─Б╠БтИЪyaj тАШattract by sacrificeтАЩ, it combines a directional preverb with a root of ritual activity, producing a portmanteau тАЬ(send) away by perfoming ritual serviceтАЩ. So Oldenberg тАШhinweghuldigenтАЩ, which he paraphrases as тАЬhonor the god such that the P─Бс╣Зis become distant.тАЭ On the syntagm y├║jy─Бya тИЪvс╣Э see comm. ad IX.88.1.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬChief leader (of rites), these praises of man addressed to you revert to us, who are the offerers of(sacrificial) riches; do you be propitious to such men, (Indra), in conflicts with enemies; be their friend, their hero,and protector.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These praises are for you, o most manly of men. Those granting bounties, inclined toward usтАФ
o Indra, become kindly disposed to them at the obstacle-smashing, as a champion who is both comrade and helper of men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

We might have expected an unaccented gen. pl. *nar─Бm in the voc. phrase with nс╣Ыtama, but donтАЩt get it. There are no unaccented occurrences of this genitive. It would be possible instead to read nar─Б╠Бm with et├й st├│m─Бс╕е (тАЬthese praises of menтАЭ), but nс╣Ы╠Бtama- + gen. pl. of nс╣Ы╠Б- is a fixed phrase, though usually with nс╣Ыс╣З─Б╠Бm (I.77.4, III.51.4, IV.25.4, etc.). I am now inclined to read nar─Б╠Бm with both st├│m─Б(с╕е) and nс╣Ыtama. It is positioned between them, adjacent to both. The published translation could be modified to тАЬThese praises of men are for you, o most manly of men.тАЭ The first gen. is subjective. Note the co-occurrence of nar─Б╠Бm, the older gen. pl. to nс╣Ы╠Б-, and the newer one nс╣Ыс╣З─Б╠Бm in this verse.

Geldner takes b as an independent nominal clause, while I consider it a sort of definitional relative clause manqu├й, that is, lacking the relative pronoun y├й which would find its referent in the initial t├йс╣г─Бm of c.

Although d looks to contain a simple conjoined NP, each of whose members consists of two members, s├бkh─Б ┼Ы┼л╠Бraс╕е and avit─Б╠Бnс╣Ыс╣З─Б╠Бm, each with a ca between the two members (so Geldner, JSK I.195), I prefer to take ┼Ы┼л╠Бraс╕е as the principal predication of Indra, with the other two terms, s├бkh─Б and avit─Б╠Бnс╣Ыс╣З─Б╠Бm, secondarily predicated of Indra as ┼Ы┼л╠Бra-. Although this introduces a minor complication in word order, the fact that ┼Ы┼л╠Бra- is overwhelmingly a noun and is used independently of Indra in the very next p─Бda (11a) persuades me that this analysis is correct, especially since both тАЬcomradeтАЭ and тАЬhelper of menтАЭ are terms that explicitly encode IndraтАЩs relationship to men, while тАЬchampionтАЭ is of a different order. The distribution of caтАЩs makes no problems for this analysis.

Thine are these lauds, O manliest of heroes, lauds which revert to us and give us riches.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHero, Indra, glorified on the present occasion, and propitiated by praise, be amplified in your person n forour protection; bestow upon us food and habitations; and do you ever cherish us wiht blessings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Now, o champion Indra, being praised by reason of your help, aroused by sacred formulations, become strengthened in your own body.
Measure out prizes to us, measure out beings [=people]. тАУ Do you
protect us always with your blessings.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The finals of p─Бdas a and c echo each other: тАж ┼лt─л╠Б# тАж ├║pa st─л╠Бn # I think it quite likely that mimihy out of sandhi should be accented (mimih├н) contra the Pp., given the balanced clausal-type constructions before and after (├║pa no v─Б╠Бj─Бn тАж ├║pa st─л╠Бn), a possibility Oldenberg raises but considers uncertain.

Griffith

Now, lauded for thine aid, Heroic Indra, sped by our prayer, wax mighty in thy body.
Apportion to us strength and habitations. Ye Gods, protect us evermore with blessings.

Geldner

Nun mach dich stark am Leibe, zur Gunsterweisung gepriesen, durch das Kraftwort angefeuert, tapferer Indra! Teil uns die Gewinne zu und Angeh├╢rige! - Beh├╝tet ihr uns immerdar mit eurem Segen!

Grassmann

Erstark am Leib nun, Indra, du gepries’ner, o Held, zur H├╝lfe durch Gebet befl├╝gelt; Miss du uns Sch├дtze zu und t├╝cht’ge Leute; ihr G├╢tter, sch├╝tzt uns stets mit eurem Segen.

(рдпреВрдпрдореН) рддреБрдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреА (рд╕рджрд╛) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ (рдкрд╛рдд) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░реЛ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╢реВрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрддрд╡рдорд╛рдиреЛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЬреВрдд рдКрддреА рддрдиреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╛рд╡реГрдзрд╕реНрд╡ рд╕реНрддреАрдиреН рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреНрди рдЙрдкрдорд┐рдореАрд╣рд┐ рдиреБ рд╕рджреНрдпрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдмрд▓рдореБрдкрдорд┐рдореАрд╣рд┐ред рд╣реЗ рднреГрддреНрдпрд╛ ! рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрдирдГ рд╕рджрд╛ рдкрд╛рдд реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдиреВ) рд╕рджреНрдпрдГред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЛрдЪрд┐ рддреБрдиреБрдШреЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░рдХ (рд╢реВрд░) рдирд┐рд░реНрднрдп рд╕реЗрдиреЗрд╢ (рд╕реНрддрд╡рдорд╛рдирдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдпреЛрджреНрдзреДрдиреН рд╡реАрд░рд░рд╕рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдиреЗрдиреЛрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣рдпрдиреН (рдКрддреА) рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЬреВрддрдГ) рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд╛ рдзрдиреЗрдирд╛рдиреНрдиреЗрди рдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ (рддрдиреНрд╡рд╛) рд╢рд░реАрд░реЗрдг (рд╡рд╛рд╡реГрдзрд╕реНрд╡) рднреГрд╢рдВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрд╕реНрд╡ (рдЙрдк) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреН) рдмрд▓рд╡реЗрдЧрд╛рджрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдиреН (рдорд┐рдореАрд╣рд┐) рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрдВ рдХреБрд░реБ (рдЙрдк) (рд╕реНрддреАрдиреН) рд╕рдВрд╣рддрд╛рдиреН рдорд┐рд▓рд┐рддрд╛рдиреН (рдпреВрдпрдореН) (рдкрд╛рдд) (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рд╕реБрдЦреИрдГ (рд╕рджрд╛) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН реерезрезрее

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╕реЗрдиреЗрд╢ ! рддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╢рд░реАрд░рдмрд▓рдВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрд╕рд┐ рддрдереИрд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдпреЛрджреНрдзреДрдгрд╛рдВ рд╢рд░реАрд░рдмрд▓рдВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдп рдпрдерд╛ рднреГрддреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖реЗрдпреБрд╕реНрддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдордкреНрдпреЗрддрд╛рдиреН рд╕рддрддрдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖реЗрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддреЗрди рд░рд╛рдЬрд╕рднрд╛рд╕реЗрдиреЗрд╢рд╛рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рд╜рдзреНрдпреЗрддреГрд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рднреГрддреНрдпрдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рд╜рдзреНрдпреЗрддреГрдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддреНрд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрдореЗрдШрдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╣реЛрддреГрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реЗрдирд╛рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддрд┐рдЧреБрдгрдХреГрддреНрдп-рд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддреНрдпреГрдЧреНрд╡реЗрджреЗ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдорд╛рд╖реНрдЯрдХреЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЛрд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрдГ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓ рдПрдХреЛрдирд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддреА ! рддреВ рдЬрд╕рд╛ рдЖрдкрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рд╢рд░реАрд░ рд╡ рдмрд▓рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдврд╡рддреЛрд╕ рддрд╕реЗрдЪ рд╕рдВрдкреВрд░реНрдг рдпреЛрджреНрдзреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╢рд░реАрд░ рд╡ рдмрд▓рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдврд╡. рдЬрд╕реЗ рд╕реЗрд╡рдХ рддреБрдЭреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддрд╕реЗ рддреВрд╣реА рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рдирд┐рд░рдВрддрд░ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░. рее резрез рее
